## Instruction Priority

Superpowers skills override default system prompt behavior, but **user instructions always take precedence**:

1. **User's explicit instructions** (CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, AGENTS.md, direct requests) — highest priority
2. **Superpowers skills** — override default system behavior where they conflict
3. **Default system prompt** — lowest priority

If CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, or AGENTS.md says "don't use TDD" and a skill says "always use TDD," follow the user's instructions. The user is in control.

## How to Access Skills

**Never read skill files manually with file tools** — always use your platform's skill-loading mechanism so the skill is properly activated.

**In Claude Code:** Use the `Skill` tool. When you invoke a skill, its content is loaded and presented to you — follow it directly.

**In Codex:** Skills load natively. Follow the instructions presented when a skill activates.

**In Copilot CLI:** Use the `skill` tool. Skills are auto-discovered from installed plugins.

**In Gemini CLI:** Skills activate via the `activate_skill` tool. Gemini loads skill metadata at session start and activates the full content on demand.

**In other environments:** Check your platform's documentation for how skills are loaded.

## Platform Adaptation

Skills speak in actions ("dispatch a subagent", "create a todo", "read a file") rather than naming any one runtime's tools. For per-platform tool equivalents and instructions-file conventions, see [claude-code-tools.md](references/claude-code-tools.md), [codex-tools.md](references/codex-tools.md), [copilot-tools.md](references/copilot-tools.md), [gemini-tools.md](references/gemini-tools.md), [pi-tools.md](references/pi-tools.md), and [antigravity-tools.md](references/antigravity-tools.md). Gemini CLI users get the tool mapping loaded automatically via GEMINI.md.

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action.** Even a 1% chance a skill might apply means that you should invoke the skill to check. If an invoked skill turns out to be wrong for the situation, you don't need to use it.

## Red Flags

These thoughts mean STOP—you're rationalizing:

| Thought | Reality |
|---------|---------|
| "This is just a simple question" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |
| "I need more context first" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |
| "Let me explore the codebase first" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |
| "I can check git/files quickly" | Files lack conversation context. Check for skills. |
| "Let me gather information first" | Skills tell you HOW to gather information. |
| "This doesn't need a formal skill" | If a skill exists, use it. |
| "I remember this skill" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |
| "This doesn't count as a task" | Action = task. Check for skills. |
| "The skill is overkill" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |
| "I'll just do this one thing first" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |
| "This feels productive" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |
| "I know what that means" | Knowing the concept ≠ using the skill. Invoke it. |

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills could apply, use this order:

1. **Process skills first** (brainstorming, systematic-debugging) - these determine HOW to approach the task
2. **Implementation skills second** (frontend-design, mcp-builder) - these guide execution

"Let's build X" → brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
"Fix this bug" → systematic-debugging first, then domain-specific skills.

## Skill Types

**Rigid** (TDD, systematic-debugging): Follow exactly. Don't adapt away discipline.

**Flexible** (patterns): Adapt principles to context.

The skill itself tells you which.

```text
Base directory for this skill: /home/light/.claude/plugins/cache/claude-plugins-official/superpowers/6.0.3/skills/brainstorming

# Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs

Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.

Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.

<HARD-GATE>
Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
</HARD-GATE>

## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"

Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.

## Checklist

You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:

1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits
2. **Offer the visual companion just-in-time** — NOT upfront. The first time a question would genuinely be clearer shown than described, offer it then (its own message); on approval its browser tab opens for you. If no visual question ever arises, never offer it. See the Visual Companion section below.
3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation
5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
7. **Spec self-review** — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
9. **Transition to implementation** — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan

## Process Flow

` ` `dot
digraph brainstorming {
    "Explore project context" [shape=box];
    "Ask clarifying questions" [shape=box];
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" [shape=box];
    "Present design sections" [shape=box];
    "User approves design?" [shape=diamond];
    "Write design doc" [shape=box];
    "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" [shape=box];
    "User reviews spec?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke writing-plans skill" [shape=doublecircle];

    "Explore project context" -> "Ask clarifying questions";
    "Ask clarifying questions" -> "Propose 2-3 approaches";
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" -> "Present design sections";
    "Present design sections" -> "User approves design?";
    "User approves design?" -> "Present design sections" [label="no, revise"];
    "User approves design?" -> "Write design doc" [label="yes"];
    "Write design doc" -> "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)";
    "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" -> "User reviews spec?";
    "User reviews spec?" -> "Write design doc" [label="changes requested"];
    "User reviews spec?" -> "Invoke writing-plans skill" [label="approved"];
}
` ` `

**The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.

## The Process

**Understanding the idea:**

- Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)
- Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., "build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.
- If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec → plan → implementation cycle.
- For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea
- Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too
- Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions
- Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria

**Exploring approaches:**

- Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs
- Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning
- Lead with your recommended option and explain why

**Presenting the design:**

- Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design
- Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced
- Ask after each section whether it looks right so far
- Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing
- Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense

**Design for isolation and clarity:**

- Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently
- For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?
- Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.
- Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.

**Working in existing codebases:**

- Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.
- Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.
- Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.

## After the Design

**Documentation:**

- Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`
  - (User preferences for spec location override this default)
- Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available
- Commit the design document to git

**Spec Self-Review:**
After writing the spec document, look at it with fresh eyes:

1. **Placeholder scan:** Any "TBD", "TODO", incomplete sections, or vague requirements? Fix them.
2. **Internal consistency:** Do any sections contradict each other? Does the architecture match the feature descriptions?
3. **Scope check:** Is this focused enough for a single implementation plan, or does it need decomposition?
4. **Ambiguity check:** Could any requirement be interpreted two different ways? If so, pick one and make it explicit.

Fix any issues inline. No need to re-review — just fix and move on.

**User Review Gate:**
After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:

> "Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan."

Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.

**Implementation:**

- Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan
- Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.

## Key Principles

- **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions
- **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible
- **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs
- **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling
- **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on
- **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense

## Visual Companion

A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool — not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.

**Offering the companion (just-in-time):** Do NOT offer it upfront. Wait until a question would genuinely be clearer shown than told — a real mockup / layout / diagram question, not merely a UI *topic*. The first time that happens, offer it then, as its own message:
> "This next part might be easier if I show you — I can put together mockups, diagrams, and comparisons in a browser tab as we go. It's still new and can be token-intensive. Want me to? I'll open it for you."

**This offer MUST be its own message.** Only the offer — no clarifying question, summary, or other content. Wait for the user's response. If they accept, start the server with `--open` so their browser opens to the first screen automatically. If they decline, continue text-only and don't offer again unless they raise it.

**Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**

- **Use the browser** for content that IS visual — mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs
- **Use the terminal** for content that is text — requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions

A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. "What does personality mean in this context?" is a conceptual question — use the terminal. "Which wizard layout works better?" is a visual question — use the browser.

If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:
`skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`
```

22	├── parameter_calc/      형상 파라미터 최적화 (v4 권위본 python_gpu_triangle/, CLAUDE.md 필독)
23	├── motor_control/       실차 런타임 제어
24	│   ├── drive/           구동 모터 (bl70200 실전 · x2212_test 테스트, ODrive USB/CAN)
25	│   ├── steering/        조향 (AK45-36 실전, CAN socketcan can0)
26	│   ├── vision/          검출·스트리밍 (YOLO26 + RealSense D435i, 모터 명령 없음)
27	│   ├── sensors/         US-100 초음파 거리 (UART /dev/ttyTHS1)
28	│   ├── safety_us100/    US-100 충돌방지 판정 (publish-only safe/warn/stop)
29	│   ├── corner_module/   코너 1개(조향+구동) 협조 제어 + DualSense 텔레옵
30	│   ├── laptop/          노트북 측 텔레옵 클라이언트
31	│   └── pi/              라즈베리파이 측 서버 (laptop/ 과 1:1 짝)
32	├── motor_gui/           웹 진단·튜닝 GUI (FastAPI + 트랜스포트 추상화, AK/ODrive CAN·USB)
33	├── docker/              컨테이너 정의 (x86 dev + Jetson Orin Nano 배포)
34	├── scripts/             호스트 헬퍼 (recv_stream.sh · recv_yolo3d.py · can_setup.sh)
35	└── docs/                설계(specs) · 계획(plans) · 보고(reports) + 대회 규정 / FSM
36	` ` `
37	
38	> 모든 모터 제어 스크립트는 `axis1` 사용으로 통일.
39	
40	---
41	
42	## 개발 환경
43	
44	코드는 호스트에 두고 컨테이너 `/workspace` 로 bind mount — 이미지를 다시 빌드하지 않고
45	수정/실행한다.
46	
47	> **실행·검증은 Jetson 에서 직접 하는 것을 우선**한다(런타임 타깃이 Jetson). x86 노트북
48	> 컨테이너 테스트(무하드웨어 `pytest` + fake 드라이버)는 **Jetson 에 접근 불가할 때의 차선책**.
49	
50	### x86 (개발·테스트)
51	
52	` ` `bash
53	xhost +local:docker                                         # cv2 창을 호스트로 띄우려면
54	docker compose -f docker/docker-compose.yml up -d --build
55	docker compose -f docker/docker-compose.yml exec powertrain bash
56	` ` `
57	
58	CPU 전용 이미지(~3.3GB, Ubuntu 22.04 + ODrive · pygame · OpenCV · ultralytics · OpenVINO).
59	코드 작성 · 단위테스트(`pytest`) · OpenVINO/CPU YOLO 용. YOLO GPU 추론은 Jetson 에서만 한다.
60	
61	### Jetson Orin Nano (배포)
62	
63	` ` `bash
64	git clone https://github.com/lightminn/power-train-sw.git && cd power-train-sw
65	sudo docker compose -f docker/docker-compose.jetson.yml up -d --build
66	sudo docker compose -f docker/docker-compose.jetson.yml exec powertrain bash
67	` ` `
68	
69	베이스 `dustynv/l4t-pytorch:r36.4.0` (CUDA + cuDNN + TensorRT + ARM PyTorch) + RealSense SDK
70	(librealsense / pyrealsense2) 소스 빌드 포함. JetPack 의 `nvidia-container-runtime` 으로 추가
71	설정 없이 동작. **Orin Nano 는 NVENC 하드웨어 인코더가 없어**(Orin NX/AGX 만 탑재) 영상은
72	SW 인코딩(`x264enc`) + SRT(ARQ 손실복구) 로 보낸다.
73	
74	### 호스트 사전 준비
75	
76	| 항목 | 내용 |
77	| --- | --- |
78	| CAN | CAN 트랙·조향 사용 전 `bash scripts/can_setup.sh` (can0 500 kbps, mttcan + devmem) |
79	| ODrive udev | `/etc/udev/rules.d/91-odrive.rules` 있어야 일반 사용자 권한으로 USB 인식 |
80	| Wayland | XWayland 가 떠 있어야 cv2 창 표시 (`echo $XDG_SESSION_TYPE` 확인) |
81	| USB 디바이스 | ODrive · DualSense · 카메라는 `/dev` 마운트로 컨테이너에 자동 노출 |
82	
83	---

113	
114	- `parameter_calc/` 수정 전 [`parameter_calc/CLAUDE.md`](parameter_calc/CLAUDE.md) 의 GPU 버그 히스토리 섹션 필독.
115	- **BL70200 트랙(HALL 모드) / X2212 트랙(엔코더 모드) 을 한 ODrive 에서 번갈아 쓰지 말 것** — NVM 에 남은 캘리 설정이 의도치 않게 적용된다(폭주/과전류). 교차 사용 시 `drive/bl70200/odrive_calibration.py` 로 모드 강제 재설정 후 시작.

118	- `motor_control/` 스크립트는 독립 실행형 원칙 유지 — 공용 모듈 분리는 사전 합의. `motor_gui` 는 `motor_control` 을 import 하되 역의존 금지.

21	| 트랙 | 풀어 쓰면 |
22	|---|---|
23	| **(A) 다리 치수 최적화** | 로커-보기 다리 길이·각도 같은 치수를 컴퓨터로 7가지 지형(계단/나무/거친지면/단턱/곡선램프/15°·30° 경사) 시뮬 돌려서 가장 잘 넘는 값으로 정함 |
24	| **(B) 로봇 제어 SW** | 모터·조향·센서·카메라·게임패드를 묶어 로봇이 굴러가게 하는 프로그램 |
25	
26	용어:
27	- **ODrive** = 구동 모터를 돌리는 제어보드.
28	- **AK40-10 / AK45-36** = 조향 모터. 테스트는 AK40, 실전은 AK45.
29	- **BL70200** = 실전 구동 모터(인휠형).
30	- **Jetson Orin Nano** = 로봇 두뇌 보드.
31	- **CAN / USB** = 두뇌와 모터를 잇는 통신선 두 종류.
32	- **YOLO** = 카메라 영상에서 물체를 자동으로 찾는 AI.

118	### Phase 1 — 기반 (하드웨어 + 골격)
119

- **Single heterogeneous CAN bus, 8 motors:** ODrive drive (standard 11-bit CANSimple frames) + AK steering (extended 29-bit VESC frames) coexisting collision-free on one 500 kbps bus, dispatched by `is_extended_id` in a single RX loop; USB-side `bl70200_setup --node --apply` self-provisions a factory ODrive (250k/node0) so it can't kill the shared bus. HIL: 8/8 independent, 0% drop at 500k vs 24–52% drop / bus-off at 1M.
- **Corner-module abstraction:** transport-agnostic actuator ABC (steer=CAN, drive=USB→CAN swappable with zero upper-layer change) + built-in safety (300ms watchdog, e-stop, 30A overcurrent trip, arm-time jump prevention via steer-target=current-angle) as the reusable 1/6 building block for a future 4WS Ackermann layer. 24 unit tests + HIL.
- **Publish-only US-100 safety verdict:** decoupled safe/warn/stop with 30mm hysteresis + fail-safe-on-3-read-failures, gating drive to zero — separation of safety-decision from actuation.
- **Alignment-free 3D coordinate fusion:** dropped full depth→color align (~108ms, 80% of loop on NVENC-less Orin Nano) for per-detection projection (2.9ms, 11mm error), split video(SRT)+coords(UDP JSON) so coordinates survive video degradation (smoke). 5.5→30fps.
- **Multi-terrain rocker-bogie geometry optimization:** 15-var / 7-terrain differential-evolution with surface-based physics, 10 weighted criteria, GPU (JAX) — f_opt 0.2004, 0.0% kinematic failure across terrains.

# Corner Module — Technical Differentiation Analysis (patent whitepaper input)

Scope read: all of `motor_control/corner_module/` (corner_module.py, actuator.py, steer_ak40.py, drive_odrive_usb.py, drive_odrive_can.py, fake.py, teleop_dualsense.py, config.py, __init__.py, README.md, tests/test_corner_module.py), plus `docs/specs/2026-05-25-corner-module-controller-design.md`, `docs/plans/2026-05-25-corner-module-controller-plan.md`, `docs/specs/2026-05-25-us100-safety-module-design.md`, and the AK CAN decode in `motor_control/steering/ak_control.py`. All paths absolute under `/home/light/ZETIN/robotics/power-train-sw/`.

## 1. Architecture — ABC layering &amp; hardware decoupling

- **Three-tier dependency inversion.** `actuator.py:9-48` defines `Actuator(ABC)` (connect/arm/disarm/tick/state/estop/close) and two refinements: `SteerActuator.set_angle(deg)` (`:39-42`) and `DriveActuator.set_velocity(turns_per_s)` (`:45-48`). `CornerModule.__init__` (`corner_module.py:15-18`) takes `steer, drive` as opaque `SteerActuator`/`DriveActuator` — it never imports a transport, an ODrive symbol, or `python-can`. The control logic is 100% written against the ABC.
- **Concrete drivers plug in behind the ABC, one per transport.** `SteerAk40` (steer over CAN/socketcan, wraps existing `ak_control.AK40`, `steer_ak40.py:20-79`), `DriveOdriveUsb` (drive over USB `odrive.find_any` → `axis1`, `drive_odrive_usb.py:32-113`), `DriveOdriveCan` (reserved CAN-only stub raising `NotImplementedError`, `drive_odrive_can.py:10-37`), and `FakeSteer`/`FakeDrive` (first-order convergence test doubles, `fake.py`). Swapping drive from USB→CAN is a one-line constructor change; control logic and tests are untouched (design doc §4.2, `:90-100`).
- **What decouples control from hardware:** (a) a **normalized telemetry dict contract** — every steer `state()` returns `{target_deg, actual_deg, cur_a, fault, stale}` and every drive `state()` returns `{target_vel, actual_vel, cur_a}`; `CornerModule.tick` consumes only these keys (`corner_module.py:81-108`), so drivers hide vendor-specific paths (e.g. USB `axis1.encoder.vel_estimate` / `motor.current_control.Iq_measured`, `drive_odrive_usb.py:96-99`; AK CAN status decode `&gt;hhhbb` → `cur_a=cur/100`, fault byte, `ak_control.py:120-126`). (b) A **`tick()` service split** — the driver, not the controller, owns command re-send + status polling each loop, so a single 50 Hz loop services two dissimilar transports non-blocking (design §4.1, `:87-88`). (c) **Strict one-way dependency**: `corner_module → steering/ak_control`; `motor_control` must not import `motor_gui` (design §3, `:62-64`) — the `state()` dict is GUI-shaped so a future adapter is additive only.

## 2. Non-trivial control mechanisms (vs a naive steer+drive combo)

**(a) State machine** — `corner_module.py`. Modes `DISCONNECTED → IDLE → ARMED → FAULT` (init `:19`; `connect`→IDLE `:31`; `arm`→ARMED `:42`; `estop`→FAULT `:70`; `disarm`→IDLE `:64`; `close`→DISCONNECTED `:75`). Two guards make it more than a label: `set()` is **rejected unless ARMED** (`:44-47`, warns + returns), and `tick()` **early-returns unless ARMED** (`:78-79`). Net effect: after a FAULT, no command or push reaches the motors until an explicit `disarm()→arm()` re-arm — commit `fd00de9` ("FAULT 재명령 방지") added this to close a review gap where FAULT could be silently re-commanded.

**(b) Watchdog** — `corner_module.py:100-102`. Each `set()` stamps `_last_set_ms` (`:50`); every tick, if `now − last_set &gt; cfg.watchdog_ms` (default **300 ms**, `config.py:15`) the **drive command is forced to 0 while steering holds its last target** (`drive_cmd = 0.0`, steer still pushed at `:111`). This is asymmetric on purpose (design §4.4.2): loss of teleop input must stop propulsion but must not snap the wheels straight. Test `test_watchdog_zeros_drive_on_timeout` injects a fake clock and asserts 3.0→0.0 across the 300 ms boundary.

**(c) E-stop** — `corner_module.py:66-70`. Calls `steer.estop()` + `drive.estop()` (both drivers command zero and drop to a safe state — ODrive `input_vel=0`→`AXIS_STATE_IDLE` `drive_odrive_usb.py:102-107`; AK `stop()` `steer_ak40.py:71-73`), zeroes the internal drive target, and latches `FAULT`. It is **corner-atomic**: a fault on *one* actuator stops *both* (design §7 "부분 실패"). Reachable from the operator (○ button, `teleop_dualsense.py:102-104`) or automatically from any tick-time trip.

**(d) Overcurrent trip** — `corner_module.py:94-97`. Supervisory software trip: `abs(st["cur_a"]) &gt; cfg.steer_current_limit_a` (default **30 A** for AK45-36, chosen conservatively vs the motor's 65 A peak; legacy AK40-10 = 5 A, `config.py:20`) → `estop()`. `cur_a` is the motor-reported Iq from the AK CAN status frame (`ak_control.py:124`), so this is a **second, independent current limit layered on top of the motor controller's own internal limit** — defense in depth against stall/scrub. Test `test_steer_overcurrent_triggers_estop` (commit `fd00de9`).

**(e) Closed-loop entry jump prevention** — the `input_pos=origin` idea, applied at two levels:
- *Driver level (drive):* `DriveOdriveUsb.arm` sets `input_vel=0` **before** requesting `AXIS_STATE_CLOSED_LOOP_CONTROL` (`drive_odrive_usb.py:58-69`) so the axis can't lurch on closed-loop entry.
- *Driver level (steer):* on `arm`, `SteerAk40` reads the **current actual output angle** and adopts it as the target (`_target_deg = self._ak.pos_out_deg`, `steer_ak40.py:39-44`) — i.e. "command = where you already are," the position analog of `input_pos=origin`.
- *Corner level (coordination):* `CornerModule.arm` (`:33-42`) orchestrates both — sets steer target = **measured** `actual_deg` and drive target = 0, pushes them, then transitions ARMED. So the corner enters closed loop with zero net demand on either axis. Verified by `test_arm_jump_prevention` (steer 15°→target 15°, drive→0).

**(f) Steering↔drive cooperation** — `corner_module.py:104-108` (the `steer_gate` policy). When `cfg.steer_gate` is on, if steering error `|target − actual| &gt; cfg.gate_deg` (default **10°**, `config.py:17-18`) the drive command is gated to 0 until the wheel finishes slewing — prevents tire scrub load and drive runaway while the corner is mid-turn. Currently **default OFF** (hook only; test `test_steer_gate_holds_drive_until_settled` proves it holds drive at 0 until `actual_deg &gt; 35°` then releases to 4.0). This is the explicit corner-level coordination that a naive "just forward both commands" controller lacks.

**(g) US-100 safety gating** — `teleop_dualsense.py:106-118`. A **publish-only** `SafetyMonitor` (independent `safety_us100` package, never touches motors) is `tick()`ed in the teleop loop; if `verdict.level == "stop"` the teleop calls `cm.set(0.0, 0.0)` instead of the joystick mapping — obstacle-proximity drive cut. Thresholds: stop ≤ **200 mm**, warn ≤ **400 mm**, hysteresis **30 mm** (release-only), `fail_stop_count` **3** (US-100 design §8). **Fail-safe by construction**: if the sensor can't be read it yields `stop` (fail-closed), and if `--no-us100` is passed the gating is skipped with an explicit ⚠️ warning (`:37-38, 84-86`). This composes with — does not replace — the watchdog/overcurrent/stale trips, giving multiple independent paths to zero-drive.

*Bonus non-obvious detail — arm-time false-stale suppression:* `SteerAk40.arm` does a `poll()` and, on success, seeds `_last_rx_ms` (`steer_ak40.py:39-44`) specifically so the **first** `CornerModule.tick` doesn't see a stale CAN window and immediately estop. This was a real HIL bug fix (commit `8e10341`, "조향 stale 버그"). The stale check itself (`:58-69`, trip if no AK status within `stale_ms`) feeds `corner_module.py:89-92` → estop.

## 3. Quantitative verification

- **Unit tests: exactly 24**, all pure-logic on fake actuators, in `tests/test_corner_module.py` (verified by count). - **Minor inconsistency flagged:** `CornerConfig.stale_ms=500` (`config.py:19`) is defined but **not wired** into the teleop's `SteerAk40(...)` construction (`teleop_dualsense.py:54`), which uses the driver's own `stale_ms=200` default. Non-blocking, but the "500 ms jitter margin" comment is not the value actually in effect.

## 4. Assessment — what is genuinely patent-differentiating vs conventional

**Conventional / textbook (weak as standalone patent claims):**
- The arm/idle/fault **state machine**, the **teleop input watchdog** (timeout→zero), **e-stop**, **clamp** on angle/velocity, and **deadzone joystick mapping** are all standard motion-control / robot-safety patterns.
- The **transport-agnostic ABC** is a straight application of dependency inversion — good engineering, but a well-known software pattern, not novel.
- **Closed-loop-entry jump prevention** (command = current position/zero velocity before enabling) is common ODrive/servo practice; obvious to a practitioner.

**Genuinely non-obvious over a generic corner controller (the defensible differentiation — it is integration/architecture, not any single mechanism):**
1. **Heterogeneous-transport corner unification under one synchronous 50 Hz tick** — CAN position steering + USB velocity drive serviced behind one ABC with per-actuator `tick()` command re-send/poll, *engineered so the drive transport can migrate USB→CAN by driver swap with zero change to control logic or tests* (`drive_odrive_can.py` reserved slot + 2 tests already asserting the contract). The explicit forward-compat to CAN-only is a concrete, documented design constraint, not an afterthought.
2. **Corner-atomic, multi-source, defense-in-depth safety composition** — four *independent* stop paths converge on one `estop()`: supervisory current trip (30 A, layered on the motor's own limit), CAN staleness, per-tick fault-byte, and (in teleop) a fail-closed publish-only ultrasonic gate — plus an asymmetric watchdog (kill propulsion, hold steering). # Patent-differentiation analysis: single-bus heterogeneous 8-motor CAN powertrain

Scope verified against source + HIL logs. Files cited are absolute-path-relative to `/home/light/ZETIN/robotics/power-train-sw/`.

## 1. Heterogeneous-bus arbitration mechanism (two protocols, one wire, no collision)

Two vendor protocols share `can0` because they live in **physically distinct CAN identifier spaces**, and the software demuxes on the IDE bit before ID:

- **AK45-36 steering (×4)** speaks the **VESC/CubeMars extended-frame** protocol (29-bit ID). `ak_control.py:85-89`: `ext_id = (packet_id &lt;&lt; 8) | motor_id`, sent `is_extended_id=True`. Packet IDs (`ak_control.py:35-39`): SET_DUTY=0, SET_BRAKE=2, SET_RPM=3, SET_ORIGIN=5, SET_POS_SPD=6, STATUS_1=41. Motor IDs = **1,2,3,4**. E.g. RPM-cmd→motor1 = `(3&lt;&lt;8)|1 = 0x301`; STATUS_1 broadcast from motor1 = `(41&lt;&lt;8)|1 = 0x2901`. RX is de-multiplexed by `pkt=(arb&gt;&gt;8)&amp;0xFF`, `nid=arb&amp;0xFF` (`ak_control.py:139-141`).
- **ODrive BL70200 drive (×4)** speaks **CANSimple standard-frame** (11-bit ID). `odrive_can_device.py:86-87` / `can_bus.py:85`: `arb = (node_id &lt;&lt; 5) | cmd_id`, sent `is_extended_id=False`. 5-bit cmd field (≤32 cmds/node: heartbeat 0x001, Get_Encoder_Estimates 0x009, Set_Input_Vel 0x00D, Set_Limits 0x00F …), 6-bit node field. Nodes = **11,12,15,16** (2 boards × dual-axis M0=axis0/M1=axis1). E.g. node11 heartbeat = `(11&lt;&lt;5)|1 = 0x161`.

Why they never collide (the load-bearing point):
1. **IDE bit separates the spaces at the hardware arbitration layer.** An 11-bit standard frame and a 29-bit extended frame are distinct identifiers even if the low 11 bits coincide; CAN arbitrates on the full ID+IDE field. Confirmed in HIL memory: *"프레임 타입(std vs ext)이 달라 arb-id 겹쳐도 무관."*
2. **CSMA/CD nondestructive bitwise arbitration** serializes all frames on the shared medium regardless of which protocol emitted them — lower ID wins, loser retransmits. No protocol-level coordination is required.
3. **Node/motor ID allocation is disjoint anyway** (AK 1-4 vs ODrive 11/12/15/16), so there is uniqueness *within* each protocol space too.
4. **Software demux is a single drain + dispatch**: one `bus.recv()` loop hands every frame to every device's `on_rx`, each of which filters its own frames by `msg.is_extended_id` then by node/motor id (`can_device.py:76-91`, `ak_device.py:87-93`, `odrive_can_device.py:191-196`).

Both device families are also configured to a matched **50 Hz periodic feedback**: AK auto-broadcasts STATUS_1 (pkt41); ODrive `can_heartbeat_rate_ms=20`→50.4 Hz. Note ODrive pos/vel/Iq are **not** auto-broadcast on this fw (`encoder_rate_ms` absent) → RTR-polled only.

## 2. Composable transport abstraction (Transport / CanDevice ABC)

Two-tier ABC in `motor_gui/backend/transport/`:

- **`Transport` ABC** (`base.py:10-51`): `connect/sample/apply/capabilities/close`, plus `device_ids/set_device_ids`. Contract deliberately trades **only JSON-serializable dicts** (`base.py:11-15`) so the web seam can later become an IPC/process boundary. Telemetry keys are namespaced `"&lt;device&gt;.&lt;signal&gt;"`.
- **`CanDevice` ABC** (`can_device.py:9-48`): one motor unit on a shared bus — `attach(bus)`, `capabilities_fragment()`, `request(bus)` (RTR poll, default no-op), `on_rx(msg)` (filter+cache own frames), `tick(bus)` (watchdog/periodic), `sample()`, `apply(bus,op,args)`, `close(bus)`, `can_id_spec()/set_can_id()`.
- **`CanTransport`** (`can_device.py:51-143`) owns **exactly one** socketcan bus and a **list of CanDevices**. Its `sample()` (`:76-91`) is the multiplex engine: (a) each device fires its RTR `request()`; (b) a **single recv-drain loop** feeds every frame to every device's `on_rx` (each self-filters); (c) each device's `tick()` runs watchdog resends; (d) fragments are merged into one namespaced telemetry dict. `apply()` routes by `target==device.name` (`:93-99`). `capabilities()` merges each device's fragment (`:101-114`). `device_ids/set_device_ids` (`:116-129`) expose per-device runtime CAN-ID reassignment.

**Drop-in a new device type** = implement the `CanDevice` ABC and append the instance to the `devices` list — nothing else changes. `AkDevice` (extended frames, `ak_device.py`) and `OdriveCanDevice` (standard frames, `odrive_can_device.py`) are exactly two such implementations coexisting in one list on one bus. This is explicitly the software building block of the 8-motor topology and the future 4WS Ackermann layer.

**Host-thread architecture** (`worker.py:20-26,183-220`): `HardwareWorker` is the **sole owner** of the Transport, running one **100 Hz** loop; the web layer touches it only via `submit/estop/latest/history/capabilities/subscribe` — so there is never concurrent bus access. Crucially the **RTR poll rate is decoupled from the 100 Hz loop**: ODrive polls at `_POLL_HZ=15` (`odrive_can_device.py:49-50,180-189`), AK watchdog resends at `_RESEND_HZ=20` (`ak_device.py:18,100-110`). This bounds host TX to keep a marginal bus out of bus-off while keeping command latency at 100 Hz (rationale documented at `odrive_can_device.py:46-50`).

## 3. Provisioning / self-healing: `bl70200_setup.py --node N --apply`

Failure mode: a **factory/reset ODrive defaults to 250 kbps + node_id 0**. Attached to the 500 k bus, its frames are misread as bit errors → `can0` goes **ERROR-PASSIVE (berr rx 127)** and the bus appears to carry phantom *"node 0 / cmd4 / dlc8 garbage @120 Hz"* (250 k frames misparsed at 500 k). A single mis-provisioned drive thus takes down the entire shared field bus.

Remediation is **out-of-band over USB** because you cannot fix the baud rate over the very CAN bus the device is breaking. `bl70200_setup.py apply()` (`:45-78`) atomically corrects **both**:
- `odrv.can.set_baud_rate(500000)` (`:69`) — note `config.baud_rate` is not directly writable, must use the method.
- `axis.config.can_node_id = N` with a nested-path fallback (`:70-73`).
- plus disables startup auto-cal (`:74-76`) and `save_configuration()` (`:77`, reboots).

`CFG` defaults node=11/baud=500000 (`:27`); `--node` (`:102-105`) lets each of the 4 boards take a distinct id (11/12/15/16) with no collision. After `--apply` the bus returns to ERROR-ACTIVE. Host-side complement: `can_setup.sh:10-11` brings `can0` up at **500 kbps + `restart-ms 100`** (bus-off auto-recovery; `restart-ms 0` would latch) **+ `txqueuelen 1000`** (absorb ENOBUFS TX backlog).

## 4. Quantitative verification (HIL)

Core comparison — 2 motors (id1/2), 10 rpm × 2 s × 10 runs = **2100 command frames**, physical harness held fixed:

| Config | Command drop | Bus-off events | Error frames | Verdict |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **1 Mbps + 100 Hz feedback** | **24–52%** (per-run 5.9→24→52%) | 15–24 | many; late TX wedge | unusable |
| **500 kbps + 50 Hz feedback** | **0.00%** (2100/2100 ACK) | 0 | 0 | clean |

- Physical layer unchanged → the fix was **2× bit-time + halved feedback traffic** creating margin (long robot harness cannot be shortened → trade bitrate/feedback-rate for margin).
- **3-device load test** (15 s, ODrive node11 + AK id1 + id2): command drop **0.000%** (1428 intended all sent, send-fail 0, error frames 0, tx_errors 0, bus-off delta 0).
- **8-motor spin test** (2026-06-29): AK 1-4 + ODrive 11/12/15/16, 1 rev each — **8/8 OK** (AK +364–365° fault0, ODrive ~1 rev err0), repeatable.
- **Bandwidth headroom model**: 500 k with 10 motors (cmd + 50 Hz feedback) ≈ 130 kbit/s ≈ **26% bus load**; 100 Hz would push ~52% (tight) → design rule = split into two CAN buses (steering/drive) at that point.
- **Termination**: 120 Ω at each of the two bus ends only (middle motors termination OFF) = **60 Ω measured across the bus** (measure with power off). `restart-ms 100`, `txqueuelen 1000`.
- **Feedback rates**: AK STATUS_1 auto-broadcast 50 Hz; ODrive heartbeat 50.4 Hz; ODrive pos/vel/Iq via RTR polling throttled to ~15 Hz.
- Electrical: 48 V (vbus ~47.6 V), UV trip 40, OV 56, brake 2.0 Ω.

(Numbers sourced from project memory `ak-can-500k-50hz`, `can-bus-multidevice-topology`, `bl70200-odrive-jetson-bringup`; corroborating design notes in `docs/specs/2026-05-23-odrive-can-gui-design.md:7-27`. The drop-rate figures live in the HIL memory, not in the checked-in docs.)

## 5. Assessment — what is patent-differentiating vs standard CAN engineering

**Likely rejected as obvious / prior art (do not anchor claims here):**
- Mere coexistence of extended (29-bit) and standard (11-bit) frames on one bus — this is baseline CAN 2.0B; the IDE bit separating spaces is by-spec.
- Lowering bitrate to gain margin on a marginal harness — textbook.
- 120 Ω dual-end termination, `restart-ms`, `txqueuelen` — standard socketcan hygiene.
- The CANSimple and VESC protocols themselves — vendor-defined.

**Genuinely non-obvious / defensible (anchor claims here):**
1. **Composable heterogeneous-device transport as an integrated system.** A single Transport aggregating an *open set* of protocol-specific `CanDevice` drivers on one socketcan bus, with a unified pipeline: per-device RTR-poll → single recv-drain demux (by IDE then id) → watchdog tick → namespaced telemetry merge → single-owner control thread, plus per-device runtime CAN-ID reassignment with reconnect. The engineering that lets two *dissimilar closed-loop control stacks* — a position-servo steering protocol and an FOC velocity/position drive protocol — share one 100 Hz control thread while **decoupling each device's poll rate** (15 Hz ODrive RTR, 20 Hz AK watchdog) to stay under bus-off is the real, reusable IP — not merely "it works once."
2. **Self-healing out-of-band provisioning.** The recognition that a factory-default node is a *single-point bus-killer* whose signature is a phantom ERROR-PASSIVE "node0/cmd4 @120 Hz garbage" storm, combined with the atomic USB baud+node correction (`--node --apply`) that makes a device *safe to attach* to a live field bus you cannot reach over CAN. Failure-mode identification + out-of-band remediation + diagnostic-signature mapping is a coherent, defensible combination.
3. **Empirical operating-point-selection method.** Holding the physical layer fixed and trading *bitrate × feedback-rate* to move a marginal long harness from 24–52% loss to 0%, backed by the quantified headroom model (26% @ 500 k/10-motor, split-threshold at 100 Hz). This reads as a *design-method* claim rather than an obvious parameter tweak.
4. **Poll-decoupled single-thread control/comms co-design.** Bounding host TX (RTR ≪ control rate) specifically to prevent bus-off on a margin bus while preserving 100 Hz command latency — a non-obvious co-design, documented as a fix for an observed 1 M bus-off mode.

**Strongest single claim**: the *integrated system* of (1)+(2)+(4) — composable heterogeneous transport + out-of-band self-healing provisioning + poll-decoupled single control thread — enabling 8 heterogeneous closed-loop motors on one 500 k bus at verified 0% drop. The bare "two protocols on one bus" fact is the weakest and should be framed only as the enabling substrate, not the invention.</result>

# Vision pipeline — patent-differentiation analysis

Files: `motor_control/vision/yolo_depth_3d.py`, `gst_stream.py`, `yolo_cuda_stream.py`, `realsense_stream.py`; `scripts/recv_yolo3d.py`, `scripts/recv_stream.sh`; `docs/plans/2026-05-08-jetson-yolo-stream-plan.md`.

## 1. 3D-coordinate fusion mechanism (align-free per-detection deprojection)

Core is `deproject_box()` at `yolo_depth_3d.py:122-147`, fed by `DepthCal` at `:99-119`.

- **Which pixel:** YOLO bbox center `cu,cv = ((x1+x2)/2, (y1+y2)/2)` (`:130`) — the color-frame pixel.
- **Depth↔color alignment is NOT done frame-wide.** Instead of `rs.align`, it projects only the bbox-center color pixel into the depth image via `rs2_project_color_pixel_to_depth_pixel(...)` (`:131-133`), using precomputed intrinsics (`di`,`ci`) + extrinsics (`c2d`,`d2c`) + depth scale captured once at stream start (`DepthCal.__init__`, `:109-119`).
- **Robust depth read:** samples a patch, not one pixel — radius `r = max(4, min(w,h)//6)` (≈ bbox center 1/3), takes **median of valid (&gt;0) depth**, requires ≥5 valid pixels else returns `None` (`:140-145`). Single-pixel depth is often 0/spiky.
- **Metric 3D:** `z = median * depth_scale` → `rs2_deproject_pixel_to_point` (depth-frame point) → `rs2_transform_point_to_point(d2c)` back into the **color frame** → `(X,Y,Z)[m]` (`:145-147`).
- **Frame convention** (`:22-23`, `:301-303`): X=right, Y=down, Z=forward; `dist=√(X²+Y²+Z²)`, azimuth `az=atan2(X,Z)`, elevation `el=atan2(-Y,Z)` in degrees. These az/el are emitted alongside XYZ — the actuation-ready form.
- **The measured justification** (`:99-106`, docstring): full `rs.align` costs **~108 ms/frame (~80% of the loop)** on Orin Nano CPU; per-detection projection costs **2.9 ms**; coordinates agree with the align path to **mean 11 mm, 95th-pctile 25 mm (within sensor noise)** — stated as verified. This ~36× reduction is the load-bearing optimization.

## 2. Dual-channel low-latency architecture

- **Split rationale** (`yolo_depth_3d.py:8-16`): video channel carries **clean color only** (boxes NOT burned in); coordinates go on a **separate UDP JSON datagram** per frame to `--host:coord-port` (default 5001; `CoordSender` `:176-192`). Reasons stated: (a) burning overlay costs H.264 compression quality; (b) receiver can reuse coords **as data** (draws boxes itself, `recv_yolo3d.py:152-176`); (c) small coord packets survive video breakup — explicitly called the **primary information source in smoke ("연막 구간 주 정보원")**; (d) depth colormap is deliberately never streamed (JET is high-frequency, starves the SW encoder's bitrate).
- **Video-before-inference** (`:278-288`): the clean frame is handed to the encoder (`writer.submit(color_img...)`) **before** `model.predict()` runs at `:290`. Comment (`:278-280`): this "subtracts inference time (~24 ms) from video latency." Coordinates, computed after inference, ride the separate channel and trail by ~1 frame — tolerated because the receiver uses **time-based loose sync**. Contrast: `yolo_cuda_stream.py:116-119` does the conventional `predict → results[0].plot() → write` (boxes burned, encode after inference).
- **Encode decoupled from loop** (`AsyncWriter`, `:195-226`): pipe `write` blocks until gst finishes encoding; running it inline would serialize capture+infer with encode and "halve fps," so it runs on a thread holding only the newest frame (drops unsent). Complemented by `latest_frames()` (`:85-96`) which drains the librealsense queue to keep camera lag ≤1 frame.
- **Loose sync + heartbeat:** receiver overlays the latest coord packet on the latest decoded frame; no frame-id matching (H.264 carries none), off-by-1–2 frames deemed fine for teleop; **STALE warning when coord packet &gt;0.7 s old** (`recv_yolo3d.py:13-16`, `:158-176`). Sender emits **empty `dets` as a heartbeat** so the receiver distinguishes "no detection" from "link dead" (`:179-180`).
- **SRT latency matching:** send `--srt-latency` default 60 ms (`:69-72`) written into `srt://:port?mode=listener&amp;latency=` (`gst_stream.py:61`); receiver `--latency` default 60 (`recv_yolo3d.py:57`, `:99`) and `recv_stream.sh` 3rd arg default 60. SRT negotiates the **max of both ends**, so both must be lowered together (30 low-latency teleop, 100–120 congested WiFi).
- **Sender=listener / receiver=caller** (`gst_stream.py:16-18`, `wait-for-connection=false`): robot serves the stream, laptop connects; receiver can die and reconnect without breaking the sender pipeline. Receiver has a stall watchdog (`select`-based, `recv_yolo3d.py:179-196`, `stall-timeout` 4 s) because `srtsrc` caller hangs without EOF on link death.

## 3. NVENC-absent adaptation (Orin Nano)

- **Hard constraint** (`gst_stream.py:4-10`): Orin Nano has **no NVENC at all** (only Orin NX/AGX); `nvv4l2h264enc` won't work under any driver/mount combo → SW encoding is the only path. Confirmed empirically in plan history issue #7 (`plan.md:645`): L4T NVENC plugin (1.14 ABI) ↔ container GStreamer 1.20+ element incompatibility, resolved by SW encode.
- **SW encoder tuning** (`:35-44`): `x264enc tune=zerolatency` (0 B-frames, slice-threaded) `speed-preset=superfast` (chosen so the 6-core A78 can coexist with YOLO) `bitrate=3000` kbps `key-int-max=30`. `openh264` fallback for images lacking plugins-ugly, with `complexity=low` (don't starve the detection loop) + `scene-change-detection=false` (suppress IDR bursts).
- **SRT ARQ tradeoff** (`:12-18`): plain UDP/RTP has no loss recovery (rtpjitterbuffer only reorders/de-jitters) → blocknoise/freeze on congested venue WiFi. SRT adds **ARQ retransmit over low-latency UDP**; the `latency` param *is* the retransmit budget — the explicit lever trading latency for loss recovery, the key mitigation for a SW-encoded stream that can't afford to also lose packets.
- **TS packaging for low latency** (`:57-63`): `mpegtsmux alignment=7` (188 B×7 SRT-payload-sized chunks), `h264parse config-interval=-1` (SPS/PPS on every keyframe → mid-join decode). Receiver forces `avdec_h264 max-threads=1` (`recv_stream.sh:25-26`, `recv_yolo3d.py:94`) because multi-thread decode injects frame-count fixed latency that amplifies at low fps.

## 4. Quantitative

- **Resolution:** yolo_depth_3d default **848×480** (D435i depth-module native res, 16:9, 30 fps lossless — `:57-60`); yolo_cuda_stream default 1280×720.
- **Model:** YOLO26n (team-standardized), conf 0.4.
- **Latency knobs:** SRT 60 ms default; x264 3000 kbps; keyint/GOP 30; coord STALE 0.7 s; stall watchdog 4 s.
- **Deprojection:** align 108 ms → per-detection 2.9 ms (~36×); coord agreement mean 11 mm / 95th-pctile 25 mm; YOLO inference ~24 ms (Orin Nano).
- **Streaming benchmark** (`plan.md:613-634`, YOLOv8n on a USB webcam — predates the D435i/YOLO26 build, so indicative not final):
  - PyTorch FP32 640×480: **23.6 fps**, infer 23.4 ms, e2e 36.9 ms
  - TensorRT FP16 640×480: **27.6 fps**, infer **9.9 ms**, e2e 33.3 ms (**TRT 2.4× faster inference**; e2e ≈ 1/30 s = SW-encode-bound, the direct NVENC-absent penalty)
  - 1280×720: PT 12.7 fps / TRT 15.9 fps
- Runtime diagnostic: per-frame `frame_age = now − rs_capture_timestamp` to detect camera-queue backlog (`:348-351`).

## 5. Assessment — what is genuinely patent-differentiating

**Strongest / genuinely non-obvious:**

1. **Align-free per-detection deprojection with quantified equivalence.** The insight "we only need depth at a few bbox centers, so skip full-frame registration" turns a 108 ms align into a 2.9 ms projection while proving 11 mm agreement. This is a concrete, measured, non-obvious systems optimization directly enabling real-time depth-fused detection on a CPU-align-bound Orin Nano — the most defensible technical claim. A conventional YOLO+RealSense demo calls `rs.align` (or `depth.get_distance` at a pixel) and eats the cost.

2. **"Video-before-inference" emission ordering.** Structurally decoupling the clean-frame encode from detection so remote-driving video latency **excludes** the ~24 ms inference — while a *separate* coordinate channel absorbs the resulting ~1-frame skew via loose time-sync — is architecturally unusual. The standard pattern (exactly what `yolo_cuda_stream.py` still does) is `plot()`-then-encode, which forces video to wait on inference and permanently fuses pixels+metadata.

3. **Split video/coordinate channels justified by loss-domain reasoning.** Clean H.264/SRT video + tiny UDP-JSON metric-coordinate packets, argued from (a) no compression penalty, (b) downstream data reuse, (c) **coordinate survival when video is lost (smoke/jamming)** with a heartbeat to disambiguate "no target" vs "link dead." For a defense robot this robustness framing is a differentiator over a single burned-in stream.

4. **Cross-team 3D supply.** Emitting metric XYZ + azimuth/elevation as a reusable machine-readable stream that can **supply or replace** the separate robot-arm team's depth-less 2D-pixel P-control is a system-integration novelty in context (though the coordinate math itself is standard).

**Conventional (do NOT over-claim as novel):** the base fusion (bbox center → depth → deproject) is textbook RealSense; patch-median depth robustness is common practice; SRT-for-video, x264 zerolatency, and TensorRT-FP16-on-Jetson are all off-the-shelf. The **NVENC-absent SW-encode + SRT-ARQ + listener-reconnect + latency-negotiation** stack is sound engineering and a coherent low-latency-over-lossy-WiFi design, but reads more as adaptation-to-constraint than invention — patentable value there is the *specific tuned combination*, not any single element.

Recommendation: anchor the patent claims on (1) align-free per-detection deprojection with the measured equivalence bound, and (2) the video-before-inference + split-channel architecture with loss-domain robustness — those are the two ideas that are both non-obvious and backed by numbers in-repo.</result>

# US-100 Collision-Avoidance Safety Module — Technical Differentiation Analysis

Files reviewed: `motor_control/safety_us100/{config,verdict,evaluator,safety_monitor,us100,fake_sensor,demo,teleop_odrive_only,__init__}.py`, `README.md`, `tests/test_safety.py`; `motor_control/sensors/us100_{basic,robust}.py`; `motor_control/corner_module/{teleop_dualsense,corner_module,config}.py`; `docs/specs/2026-05-25-us100-safety-module-design.md`; `docs/plans/2026-05-25-us100-safety-module-plan.md`.

## 1. Architecture — publish-only / separation of concerns

- **Verdict is a value, not an action.** The module's only output is an immutable `Verdict(level, distance_mm)` frozen dataclass (`verdict.py:9-13`). Nothing in `safety_us100/` imports `odrive`, CAN, or any actuator (the one exception, `teleop_odrive_only.py`, is a *consumer/demo* app, not the safety core). The safety core physically cannot command a motor — decoupling is enforced by dependency structure, not convention.
- **Three-layer split, hardware-isolated:** pure decision (`evaluator.evaluate()`, `evaluator.py:6-35`) ← state/latching (`SafetyMonitor.tick/verdict`, `safety_monitor.py:12-26`) ← hardware I/O (`Us100Sensor.read`, `us100.py:20-37`). The decision layer is a **pure function** — no I/O, no globals, deterministic in `(distance, cfg, prev_level)`. This is the certifiability lever: the safety logic is fully exercisable without hardware and without a running control loop.
- **Consumers pull, module never pushes.** Design doc states the module "does not touch `corner_module` or `motor_gui`" (`design.md:129-131`). Consumers call `monitor.tick()` then read `monitor.verdict()` in their own loop — no background thread, no callbacks into actuation (`design.md:189-192`).
- **Dual-channel verdict** carries *both* the level and the raw distance, with `distance_mm=None` reserved for "unreadable" (`verdict.py:12`, `design.md:150-151`). A consumer can therefore distinguish "STOP because obstacle at 150 mm" from "STOP because the sensor is dead" (`level==STOP &amp;&amp; distance_mm is None`) from a single object — relevant to fault annunciation/logging in a safety case.
- **Why it matters for certification:** the actuation-side estop paths (watchdog, overcurrent, CAN-stale in `corner_module.py:84-108`) are independent of the ultrasonic verdict. The verdict is one *advisory input* to an actuator state machine that has its own orthogonal safety trips — a defense-in-depth layering where no single component both senses and actuates.

## 2. Mechanisms

**Verdict state machine (`evaluator.py:6-35`), thresholds from `config.py:6-11` (stop=200 mm, warn=400 mm, hyst=30 mm):**
- Raw banding: `≤200→STOP`, `≤400→WARN`, else `SAFE` (`evaluator.py:10-15`).
- **Asymmetric/directional hysteresis** — the load-bearing safety property:
  - *Escalation toward danger is immediate*: `if _DANGER[raw] &gt;= _DANGER[prev]: return raw` (`evaluator.py:20-21`) — any reading ≤200 mm forces STOP instantly regardless of prior state; no debounce delays a danger transition.
  - *De-escalation toward safe requires a +30 mm margin*: releasing STOP needs distance &gt; `stop_mm+hyst = 230 mm` to reach WARN, and &gt; `warn_mm+hyst = 430 mm` to reach SAFE (`evaluator.py:23-33`). So the 200–230 mm band **holds STOP** and 400–430 mm **holds WARN**, killing chatter when the target hovers on a threshold. Verified by `test_no_chatter_with_hysteresis` (readings 150→210→190→210 all yield STOP, `test_safety.py:136-142`).
- **Fail-safe on read failure (`safety_monitor.py:12-23`):** `None` reading increments `_fail_count`; last good verdict is *held* for transient misses, but on `_fail_count &gt;= fail_stop_count` (=3) the verdict latches `STOP, distance=None` (`safety_monitor.py:15-19`). Additionally the monitor **constructs in STOP** (`safety_monitor.py:10`) — fail-safe *before the first read*, so an unstarted or never-successfully-read sensor never reports SAFE. `evaluate(None,…)` also independently returns STOP (`evaluator.py:7-8`). Two layers of "unknown ⇒ stop."
- **0xFF-prefix UART robustness (`us100.py:26`, mirrors `sensors/us100_robust.py:10-14`):** On the Jetson Orin `/dev/ttyTHS1`, the first byte of a UART TX burst is corrupted (TX-line glitch as the line transitions out of idle). Sending the trigger `0x55` alone yields a garbled request and no/garbage reply. The fix prepends **eight `0xFF` dummy bytes** before `0x55`: `0xFF` holds the line at the idle (mark) voltage so the corruption is absorbed by throw-away bytes the sensor ignores, and the real `0x55` trigger arrives intact. Reply parsing takes the **last two bytes** of the RX buffer (`us100.py:31`, `high*256+low`), which is robust to any leading dummy echo/noise, and range-gates to 20–4000 mm (`us100.py:33-34`) — out-of-range or short reads return `None`, feeding the fail-safe path. (Contrast the naive `us100_basic.py:15-16`, which sends bare `0x55` and is the version that exhibits the corruption.)

## 3. Gating — how STOP zeroes drive

- Real integration is `corner_module/teleop_dualsense.py` (US-100 ON by default; `--no-us100` disables gating, `:37-43`).
- Per loop iteration: `monitor.tick()` → `verdict = monitor.verdict()` (`:109-110`), then the gate: `if verdict is not None and verdict.level == "stop": cm.set(0.0, 0.0)` else pass mapped stick input (`:113-116`).
- `CornerModule.set()` clamps and stores the target (`corner_module.py:44-50`); `cm.tick()` pushes `drive.set_velocity(drive_cmd)` to the ODrive (`corner_module.py:112`). So a STOP verdict overrides operator throttle with a commanded **0 turns/s** — it does not disarm/trip; it holds the drive at zero and auto-resumes when the verdict clears (soft gate). The standalone `teleop_odrive_only.py:91-93` instead *disarms* on STOP (hard latch to IDLE) — two documented gating policies.
- Independent of the ultrasonic gate, the corner-module `tick()` still enforces its own estops every cycle: steer fault, CAN-stale, overcurrent (`corner_module.py:84-97`), a **300 ms input watchdog** that zeros drive on stale teleop input (`corner_module.py:101-102`, `config.py:15`), and a steer-follow gate (`corner_module.py:105-108`).

## 4. Quantitative verification

- **22 automated unit tests**, all pass (`grep -c` = 22; plan `plan.md:759-761` expects "22 passed"). Coverage: level banding (safe/warn/stop), `None→STOP`, **immediate escalation** (`test_escalation_is_immediate`), hysteresis-hold at 210 mm and 410 mm and release at 250/440 mm (`test_safety.py:53-66`), transient-fail hold vs **3-consecutive-fail latch** (`:108-125`), initial-STOP, recovery, no-chatter, verdict schema.
- The hardware read path (`us100.py`) is intentionally *not* unit-tested (needs the physical sensor); verified by eye via `demo.py` and on real hardware per `plan.md` Task 5 Step 3.
- **Thresholds/params (config.py):** stop 200 mm, warn 400 mm, hysteresis 30 mm, fail_stop_count 3, 9600 baud, `/dev/ttyTHS1`. Sensor valid window 20–4000 mm (`us100.py:33`).
- **Timing:** control loop nominal 50 Hz (`config.py:16`, period 20 ms). **Caveat/footgun:** `us100.read()` contains a blocking `time.sleep(0.1)` (`us100.py:27`), and `monitor.tick()` runs inline in the single-threaded teleop loop — so with US-100 enabled the effective loop rate collapses to ~10 Hz, and worst-case latency from "sensor goes dead" to latched STOP is `fail_stop_count × ~100 ms ≈ 300 ms`. Obstacle-present STOP is one read cycle (~100 ms). This blocking coupling is a genuine limitation for any hard-real-time safety claim and should be disclosed, not hidden.

## 5. Assessment — patent-differentiating vs conventional ultrasonic e-stop

A conventional ultrasonic e-stop is a single distance threshold wired (often in hardware) to cut motor power — stateless, sensor-coupled-to-actuator, one channel. Against that baseline:

**Genuinely defensible / non-obvious-in-combination:**
- **Directional (asymmetric) hysteresis on a safety verdict** — zero-delay danger escalation but margin-gated release (`evaluator.py:20-33`). Direction-dependent rather than a symmetric Schmitt band; the asymmetry is the safety-relevant twist (never delay a stop, only delay a go).
- **Single immutable dual-channel verdict that is None-distinguishable** (`verdict.py`, `distance_mm=None` ⇒ sensor-fault vs obstacle-stop), letting one advisory object encode both "how close" and "do I even trust this" — supports downstream fault annunciation without a second signal path.
- **Multi-sample fail-safe latch with a fail-safe *initial* state** (STOP at construction + 3-strike latch, `safety_monitor.py:10,15-19`) — debounced against US-100's known dropout without ever transiently reporting SAFE on an uninitialized/dead sensor.
- **Defense-in-depth layering:** advisory ultrasonic verdict is *one* input to an actuator FSM carrying orthogonal, independently-triggered estops (watchdog/overcurrent/CAN-stale), with US-100 explicitly positioned as an **auxiliary** channel redundant to the primary RealSense D435i ranging (sensor diversity). The system-level claim (heterogeneous-sensor, publish-only advisory + independent actuator trips) is stronger than any single mechanism.

**Not differentiating on its own (skilled-practitioner engineering, standard functional-safety practice — IEC 61508 / ISO 13849 idioms):**
- Fail-safe-default, hysteresis, and input debouncing individually are textbook safety patterns.
- The publish-only / sense-decide-vs-act split is good architecture but conceptually a safety-verdict bus, well-precedented in safety-rated controllers.
- The **0xFF-prefix UART fix** is a real, clever, platform-specific workaround (Jetson TX first-byte corruption) — but it is a robustness hack, better protected as **trade secret / know-how** than as patent subject matter; it solves a vendor UART quirk rather than embodying an inventive step.

**Bottom line for the whitepaper:** frame the claim around the *combination and system context* — a hardware-decoupled pure-function verdict engine emitting an immutable, fault-distinguishable, directionally-hysteretic advisory that is consumed (not imposed) by a cooperative steer+drive corner-module FSM with its own independent estop stack, atop heterogeneous (ultrasonic-auxiliary + RGB-D-primary) ranging. Each individual mechanism reads as competent conventional safety engineering; the potentially non-obvious argument lives in the specific integration and the directional-hysteresis + None-distinguishable-verdict pairing. Be prepared to concede novelty on the individual patterns, and to disclose the ~10 Hz blocking-read latency coupling as a known limitation.</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>65307</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>26</tool_uses><duration_ms>166064</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>

# Whitepaper Report — Geometry Parameter Optimization Track (v4 authoritative)

Source files rooted at `/home/light/ZETIN/robotics/power-train-sw/parameter_calc/`. Authoritative code = `python_gpu_triangle/`; final result pkl = `python/zetin_optimal_params_v4.pkl` (confirmed **f_opt = 0.20035807598898847 ≈ 0.2004**, version `v4_triangle_search`, rocker=frame / bogie=triangle).

## 1. Optimization Formulation

**Mixed-integer, 15-dimensional design vector** (`ZETIN_JointOptSearch_v4_gpu.py:540-541` bounds; decode at `:177-216`):

- **2 discrete topology selectors** (the non-obvious part):
  - `x[0]` rocker_mode ∈ {1=triangle, 2=frame(parallelogram)}
  - `x[1]` bogie_mode ∈ {1=triangle, 2=frame}
  - → 4 kinematic-topology combinations searched *simultaneously* (v3 fixed both to "frame").
- **13 continuous geometric variables**, slot-shared between the two topologies:
  - Rocker: `x[2..7]` = {T_r, S_r1, α_r°} (triangle) or {T_r, S_r1, th_r1°, th_r2°, j_r} (frame; j_r = pivot split ratio 0.30–0.70). Note S_r2 is *derived*, not free (`:211`).
  - Bogie: `x[8..13]` = {L_b1, L_b2, β_b°} (triangle) or {T_b, S_b1, S_b2×5mm, th_b1°, th_b2°, j_b} (frame).
  - `x[14]` brk_v = bracket-pivot→wheel-axle vertical offset ∈ [0.345, 0.375] m (new in v4).

**Terrains (7 scored + flat feasibility gate = 8 cached)** (`gen_terrain.py`): real_stairs (3×80 mm), wood_block (90 mm blocks, 5 random heights), rough (3-sinusoid synthesis), step, curved_ramp (raised-cosine bump), incline_15°, incline_30°.

**Multi-criteria objective** (`:339-519`) — 10 criteria, weights sum to 1.0 (`W`, `:109-113`):
`stab 0.18` (largest) · `tau 0.12` · `sat 0.12` · `slip 0.12` · `cont 0.10` · `fail 0.10` · `imbal 0.08` · `sn 0.06` · `batt 0.06` · `stuck 0.06`. These are physically grounded and go well beyond torque: peak torque/TAU_REF(15 Nm); normal-force imbalance across 3 wheels; ZMP/Tip-Over-Index + liftoff; torque signal-to-noise (ride smoothness, dB); IK convergence-failure rate; **speed-aware motor saturation vs the actual τ–ω curve**; traction slip = F/(μN) with **per-terrain μ**; **continuous/thermal RMS torque vs 22 Nm rated**; **battery current vs 30 A**; **system-level "stuck" traction insufficiency**.

**Terrain aggregation is hybrid** — terrain-weighted sum for torque/imbal/sn/sat/slip/cont/stuck/batt (`W_terrain`: stairs **0.45**, rough 0.13, wood 0.12, step 0.10, curved_ramp 0.10, incline_15/30 0.05 each; `:465-466`) *plus* worst-case-over-terrain for stability (`global_toi_min = min`, `global_liftoff = max`, `:468-476`) and for saturation/thermal/battery peaks (`:483-510`). Hard-constraint gating returns large penalties for W_bot∉[400,700] mm, P0 height&gt;900 mm, rocker-bogie spacing&lt;250 mm, collision, liftoff&gt;2%, fail-rate&gt;10% (`:347-463`).

**Optimizer**: scipy `differential_evolution`, maxiter 2000, popsize 30, tol 1e-4, seed 2026, **polish=False** (L-BFGS disabled because x[0],x[1] are discrete) (`:559-564`). Actual run: 955 DE steps, 430,200 evaluations.

## 2. Physics Model

**"면-기준" = lateral-half (side-view) consistency correction** (`calc_dynamics_jax.py:208-217`, `:312-314`, `:341-345`). The sim is a 2-D side view = one lateral half of the 6-wheel robot (3 wheels Wf/Wm/Wr), left/right symmetry assumed. Because each model wheel is compared against a *per-motor* torque limit, one side must statically carry **half** the robot: `W_side = 0.5·mass·g`, `mass_side = 0.5·mass`. Normal forces, vertical inertia, and stuck-demand all use the half scale; drive force/torque/energy/current stay numerically identical (0.5·W substitution cancels a removed /2). The payoff: `slip = F_demand/(μ·N)` becomes the correct face-based slip ratio — the earlier initial-v4 used full W for N and was **~2× optimistic on slip** (invalidated its 0.2624 pkl, forcing re-run). Guard invariant: flat-cruise ΣN ≈ 0.5·mg (`test_v4.py:213-228`).

**Finite-wheel contact (two layers, not point contact)** (`calc_envelope_jax.py`): (a) **Minkowski dilation** of terrain by wheel radius — envelope `y_env(i) = max over neighbors of [y_t + √(R_w² − Δx²)]` (`:11-24`), i.e. the locus of the wheel *center* rolling as a disc over the profile; (b) **contact-patch box-car smoothing** over `patch_width≈30 mm` (`:60-68`) so the tire arc absorbs sub-patch asperities. IK constrains wheel axles onto this envelope (`ceq_jax.py:23-32`).

**Scoring pipeline for one candidate on one terrain** (`objective` `:402-454`): decode→gate→pack 21-elem p_arr → pull cached (raw 8000-pt terrain, envelope) → **adaptive_xa** samples N_PTS=100 body positions with density biased toward step edges via inverse-CDF of terrain gradient (edge_boost 3×, `:128-163`) → **kin_sim_gpu** inverse kinematics solves [y0, rocker_angle, bogie_angle] per sample so all 3 axles sit on envelope → **calc_dynamics** (trapezoidal v(x) profile, CG/link angular accel via dy/dx·v chain, lever-arm normal-force split ratio_rb=a_eff/b_eff &amp; ratio_fm, Hertzian edge impact k=1e5, per-wheel motor torque, slip, τ–ω saturation `:109-126`, RMS thermal, battery current, system stuck) → **calc_stability** (ZMP, TOI, liftoff, body-segment vs raw-terrain collision) → **calc_metrics** (torque/height S/N in dB). It is **quasi-static + inertial correction**, not full time-domain (v5 planned); a MuJoCo cross-validator exists (`validate_mujoco.py`, `cross_validate.py`) to quantify fidelity.

## 3. GPU Acceleration Strategy

- **JAX/CUDA vectorization** (`newton_solver.py`): the batched Newton IK runs all N sample points in parallel via `jax.vmap` (vs sequential `lax.scan`), with an **analytic Jacobian via `jax.jacfwd`** (float32-safe; ~3 ceq evals vs 6 for numeric central-difference; `:32-86`). Forward kinematics uses `jax.lax.switch` so **all 4 topology combos compile once** (`wpos_jax.py:152-169`) — no per-mode recompilation. 3-stage failure recovery (parallel retry → interp → CPU fsolve).
- **Envelope cache — the key algorithmic speedup** (`:308-332`): `gen_terrain` depends only on `obs_h`; `calc_envelope` only on `R_w`, `patch_width` — all **constant w.r.t. the 15 design variables** (decode_x changes only linkage geometry). So the 8-terrain × 8000-point O(N²) Minkowski envelope is computed **once at startup and reused across all ~430,200 DE evaluations**, with identical results. Eval-grid also reduced 160→100 points while the envelope stays dense 8000.

## 4. Quantitative Summary

- Dimensionality: **15** (2 discrete topology + 13 continuous); **4** topology combinations; **7** scored terrains (8 cached).
- Objective: **10** weighted criteria, **7** terrain weights (both sum to 1.0).
- **f_opt = 0.2004** (exact 0.20035807598898847). Initial v4 (pre-correction) = 0.2624 (archived). v3 = 14-dim/4-terrain, pkl 0.2624.
- Convergence: step1 0.5549 → step2 0.2674 → step948 0.200359 → held to step955.
- Compute: NVIDIA **A10 GPU, 701.7 min ≈ 11.7 h, 430,200 evals, 955 DE steps** (SLURM job 654551, clean run).
- Validation: `test_v4.py` = **38 static `check()` lines → 48 runtime assertions** (loops over 3 torque keys + 9 terrains); anchor guard = flat ΣN ≈ 0.5·mg to catch weight-frame regressions.
- Optimal geometry: Rocker=frame (T_r 390.2, S_r1 150.0, S_r2 472.1 mm, th_r1 32.3°, th_r2 35.0°, j_r 0.70); Bogie=triangle (L_b1 331.1, L_b2 331.6 mm, β_b 103.5°, W_bot 520.4 mm); brk_v 355.8 mm.
- No stated speedup multiplier vs CPU; the envelope-cache win is qualitative ("O(N²) envelope for 8 terrains done once instead of 430k times").

## 5. Assessment — Patent Differentiation

**Genuinely non-obvious / defensible:**
1. **Joint topology + dimension co-optimization** — the *mechanism topology* of both rocker and bogie (triangle vs frame-parallelogram) are optimization variables, not fixed a priori, searched jointly with 13 continuous dims in one mixed-integer DE run. Made tractable by single `lax.switch` compilation. Standard design-optimization fixes the topology then tunes lengths; searching topology *and* geometry together over terrain-averaged multi-physics cost is the strongest claim.
2. **Powertrain-reality-coupled geometry selection** — folding the real BL70200 τ–ω saturation curve, continuous/thermal RMS limit (22 Nm), and battery current limit (30 A) directly into geometry scoring, so link geometry is chosen against actuator electrical/thermal envelopes, not just kinematics/torque.
3. **면-기준 half-model consistency correction** — recognizing per-motor limits require half-weight normal forces and correcting a 2× slip optimism; a subtle, documented fidelity claim with a regression-guard test.
4. **Finite-radius contact via Minkowski envelope + contact-patch smoothing + inverse-CDF edge-biased sampling** — disc-contact locus and concentrated sampling at step edges, tuned to rocker-bogie stair traversal.
5. **Hybrid terrain-weighted-sum + worst-case aggregation** with stairs at 45% and 10 physically distinct criteria (ZMP/TOI, slip w/ per-terrain μ, ride S/N, stuck).

**Standard / weaker for patent (don't over-claim):** off-the-shelf `differential_evolution`; textbook quasi-static force balance, ZMP, Tip-Over-Index; JAX vmap/JIT vectorization and precomputing an evaluation-invariant quantity (the envelope cache) are good HPC engineering but conventional; trapezoidal velocity profile and Hertzian impulse are standard.

**Honesty caveats to carry into the whitepaper:** optimized at **mass = 50 kg** while measured mass is **~86 kg** (no re-optimization done); model is **quasi-static** (time-domain v5 only designed, not run), though a MuJoCo cross-validation harness exists to bound fidelity.</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>94366</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>17</tool_uses><duration_ms>188280</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>
```

개별 메커니즘 다수는 종래기술입니다. **신규성은 시스템 통합과 "측정된 비자명 조합"에 있고, 청구는 조합/시스템 중심으로 설계**해야 등록 가능성이 높습니다. 요소 강도 랭킹:

|---|---|---|---|

메인 청구 = 이 다섯을 상호 제약 전파하도록 수직 통합한 **1건(umbrella)**.

## 증거

**결과 로그가 명시적으로 "안 함"이라고 적혀 있습니다:**
- `docs/reports/2026-06-01-param-v4-result-log.md:95` — *"mass = **50 kg** 가정으로 실행됨 (실측 86 kg 재최적화는 하지 않기로 함)."*

**코드·결과파일도 전부 50 kg:**
- `python_gpu_triangle/ZETIN_JointOptSearch_v4_gpu.py:60` → `'mass': 50` (테스트 `test_v4.py:44`도 동일)
- 결과 pkl은 `zetin_optimal_params_v4.pkl`(2026-06-01, 50 kg) 하나뿐 + phase/smoke 중간본. **86 kg·100 kg 결과 파일은 없음.** 파라미터 폴더 최신 파일 mtime이 6/4에서 멈춰 있음.
- git 커밋에도 무게 재최적화 커밋 없음.
- Notion 페이지(방금 재조회)도 여전히 "50 kg 기준 … 86 kg 재최적화는 추후 예정."

## 두 가지 "재최적화" 구분

| | 무엇 | 상태 | 제 백서 반영 |
|---|---|---|---|
| **(A) 물리 수정 재실행** | 면-기준 물리 버그(미끄럼 2× 낙관) 수정 → **f_opt 0.2624 → 0.2004** | ✅ **됨·커밋됨** (초기본은 `archive/`로) | ✅ 이미 0.2004를 현재값으로, 0.2624를 폐기본으로 반영 |
| **(B) 무게 재최적화** | 50 kg → 실측 86 kg 기준 재실행 | ❌ **"하지 않기로 함"**(로그 명시) | §8에 "미완"으로 기재 |

즉 **"수정된 버전이 올라가 있다" = (A) 면-기준 0.2004 수정본**이고, 이건 제 백서가 이미 반영하고 있습니다. 제 §8 한계 항목은 오직 **(B) 무게 기준(50 kg)** 만 지적한 것이라, 현재 증거와는 일치합니다.

## 그래서 — 확인 부탁

혹시 제가 못 보는 곳에 **(B) 86/100 kg 재최적화 결과**가 있을 가능성:
- `parameter_calc/`는 원래 **개발 서버에서 내려받은 것**이라, 서버에서 86 kg로 다시 돌린 결과가 **이 레포엔 아직 sync 안 됐을** 수 있습니다.
- 아니면 제가 안 본 다른 Notion 페이지/버전일 수도 있고요.

**둘 중 뭐일까요?**
1. **"내가 말한 건 (A) 0.2624→0.2004 수정본이었다"** → 그럼 백서는 이미 맞습니다. §8 문구만 "물리 수정 재실행은 완료, 무게(50 kg) 재최적화만 추후"로 더 명확히 다듬을게요.
2. **"(B) 86 kg 재실행 결과가 서버/다른 데 있다"** → 그 pkl 경로나 Notion 링크(또는 새 f_opt 값)를 주시면, 그 수치로 §2.1·§4.4·§6·§8을 갱신하겠습니다.

어느 쪽인지 알려주시면 바로 반영하겠습니다. (증거상으로는 1번으로 보입니다.)
```

# typst-author skill

## Overview

This skill helps agents generate, edit, and reason about Typst documents. It provides quick‑start examples, detailed workflows, and links to the full Typst documentation (guides, tutorials, reference).

## Minimal document example

` ` `typst
#set document(title: "My Document", author: "Author Name")
#set page(numbering: "1")
#set text(lang: "en")

// Enable paragraph justification and character-level justification
#set par(
  justify: true,
